    Introduction

    Welcome to the SkyView API. The SkyView API provides client systems with key status and event notifications that are generated by the SkyView CUAS detection and tracking system. The API uses secure socket technology (TLS) to provide SkyView data to client applications in an easy-to-consume JSON format. The SkyView API is available on all current generation SkyView CUAS systems including SkyView-MPV2, SkyView-DIV2, SkyView-DIVR, SkyView-MPV3, SkyView-DIVR MKII.

    Although there are several message types published by the SkyView API for DIV2/DIVR/DIVR MKII/MPV2/MPV3 sensors, the primary content of interest is detection events which are published DetectionPublication messages. For context, it is useful to know that SkyView sensors can produce 3 basic types of detections that will have varyling levels of precision and directional information.

    Fact-Of Detection: A fact-of detection is where the sensor can confidently detect and characterize the signal (e.g., technology type and frequency information), but there is no locational information. This detection might occur for any of our systems (MPV2/DIV2/DIVR). For example, SkyView may produce an initial OMNI detection from a DI system, and for some reason the sector canâ€™t isolate (not common, but technically possible).

    Directional-Indication Detection: SkyView fixed-site systems (DIV2/DIVR/DIVR MKII) can further isolate fact-of detections to a 45-degree sector. The MPV2 will never produce a sector (only fact-of or precision). The SkyView API shares this data as a sector number from 1-8.
    Depending on the type of system, the center of sector 1 will either face true north, or be offset by 22.5 degrees.
    DIV2 and DIVR Systems show the center of sector 1 as North. DIVR MKII systems show the center of sector 1 22.5 degrees offset from true north. This change was made with DIVR MKII to support both split radome features where sectors 7,8,1,2 can be mounted mid-mast (or the front of a vechicle) and sectors 6,5,4,3 can be mounted opposite mast (or the rear of a vehicle).

    NOTE: at this time, when DIVR MKII is vehicle mounted there is no offset calculation applied to adjust for vehicle heading. This feature may be added in a future software release. As implemented, the sensor assumes it is always facing true north.

    DIVR / DIV2 Sector Alignment DIVR MKII Sector Alignment

    Precision Detection: This is a very detailed detection event that leverages our knowledge of internals for various sUAS technologies. The key drivers to if SkyView can produce a precision result (lat/lon, serial numbers, etc.) is technology type and RF characteristics. For example, SkyView can extract precision information for DJI OcuSync sUAS, but only directional or fact-of detections for these technologies at the far end of our detection range (e.g., fact-of at 20km, precision at 6km). The MPV2 example messages in this guide have precision examples of the signatures where this data exists. Unique IDs/serial numbers, specific model numbers, health and status telemetry, as well as precise 3D location information (pilot, home, and UAS position LAT/LON) are examples of the granular data that may appear in precision detection records.

    Networking

    SkyView API clients must be able to route to the SkyView CUAS system's network address. SkyView CUAS systems ship with a default IP address of 192.168.1.217. The SkyView API client can make use of any non-conflicting address on this default subnet.

    The default network configuration can be changed for unique applications using SkyView's web-based aministration console which is detailed in the Web-Based Aministrator's Guide for your SkyView system. You can specify IP, Subnet, Gateway, DNS, Hostname settings as required. Always remember to document all network changes!

    The SkyView API secure socket port is fixed at 59898. Ensure that your target network is configured to enable this port for API traffic. Client API logic should establish a buffer size of 8192 bytes (or more) to accommodate the entire contents of a SkyView API publication.

    Authentication

    Simple openssl syntax to connect to SkyView's SSL/TLS API:

    # openssl client example where the skyview IP address is modified and the cert, key, and keypass are replaced with organization-unique 
# resources obtained from Verus
openssl s_client -connect SKYVIEW_IP_ADDRESS:59898 -cert VERUS_PROVIDED_CERT -key VERUS_PROVIDED_KEY -tls1_2 -pass pass:VERUS_PROVIDED_PASS

    The SkyView API uses secure sockets (TLS) for all publications. The API consumer must have valid keys and credentials to receive SkyView API content. To obtain SkyView API keys, please contact Blue Halo at skyviewhelp@bluehalo.com.

    In addition to organization unique keys and credentials, Verus can provide a simple TCP sample client as part of our API developer's resource pack. The sample client simply parameterizes the various openssl settings to establish a valid connection. To immediately work with the SkyView API, you can make use of the provided openssl example.

    Commands

    The SkyView API has a number of client commands that can be issued to determine what messages are published. Once connected, an API client can publish one of the valid JSON formatted command strings to enable/disable message types that will be published over the socket API. It is recommended that all commands should be sent on a single line with no "new line" (\r) or "carriage reutrn" (\n) characters in the body of the message. Send a single "newline" (\n) character at the end of the message to indicate that data entry for the command is complete. If no commands are issued by the API client, only the default messages will be sent to the client (Technique and Detection Publiciations). Details of each command and default settings is provided below.

    New for API Version 2.5.9/2.6.9/3.0.9

    • blinkerBrightnessSet commands have been added.

    New for API Version 2.5.14/2.6.14/3.0.14

    • getSignalStates and signalStates commands have been added.

    Once connected, push one of the valid JSON commands to enable/disable an API message type (example enables GPS Status). If sending commands via code, be sure to send the "\n" character to signify the end of the command:

    # Command to enable GPS status messages

    {"gpsStatusEnabled":true}
    Command Default Description
    {"techniqueStatusEnabled":false} true If set to true, technique status notifications will be published.
    {"detectionStatusEnabled":false} true If set to true, DetectionPublication messages will be published for each new dettection.
    {"gpsStatusEnabled":false} false If set to true, GPS status notifications will be published.
    {"heartbeatEnabled":false} false If set to true, ConnectionStatus message will be published every 60 seconds.
    {"errorStatusEnabled":false} false If set to true, SdrErrorNotifications messages will be published if errors occur.
    {"transmitLockout":false} false If set to true, detection processing will be disabled on the SkyView sensor until either reboot, or a new command is set to "transmitLockout":false. The intent of this command is to allow an API client to disable processing while activating an out-of-band transmitter such as a jammer.
    {"performanceMetricsEnabled":false} false If set to true, system performance metrics will be sent every 60 seconds. Default is 'false'
    {"blinkerBrightnessSet":"HIGH"}
    {"blinkerBrightnessSet":"MED"}
    {"blinkerBrightnessSet":"LOW"}
    {"blinkerBrightnessSet":"OFF"}
    		 HIGH Will change the brightness intensity of the USB blinker for MPV2/MPV3 systems. Default is 'HIGH'
    NOTE: current blinker brightness value is available via the ConnectionStatus Object (blinkerBrightness).
    {"getSignalStates":true} N/A Will return a signalStates json object indicating the current enablement state of each possible detector. This message can be augmented (in full or partial) and then sent back to the SkyView to set the enablement state of individual or a group of signals through the signalStates command.
    {"signalStates":[
      {"name":"autelevo","enabled":false},
      {"name":"autelskylink","enabled":false}
    ]}
    		 N/A Sets the enablement values of individual signals. Either a full signalStates or a partial (just the signals being changed) array of signals can be sent in. If successful, a full signalStates object will be returned. if failure, errors will be returned similar to:
    {"errorCode": 2,
    "errorText":" jq - parse error: Invalid literal at line 1, column 93"}
    {"error":"bad request processing signalStates command"}
    or
    {"errorCode": 5,
    "errorText":" supplied technique name does not exists in current configuration list: {"name":"badTechniqueName","enabled":false}"}
    {"error":"bad request processing signalStates command"}

    Messages

    The SkyView API publishes a variety of messages to API clients based on requested topics (see commands). A description and example of the SkyView API messages are provided in this section.

    ConnectionStatus

    Sample ConnectionStatus publication from SkyView API:

    
{
 "ConnectionStatus": {
 "systemSerial": "SVMPV2-0250",
 "systemName": "SVMPV2",
 "systemVersion": "2.5.8",
 "sessionId": "83bd7e57-2b57-428e-a418-f6c5ad41b9cc",
 "clientId": "CN=skyview-client.customerco.com",
 "blinkerBrightness": "OFF",
 "detectionStatusEnabled": true,
 "errorStatusEnabled": true,
 "techniqueStatusEnabled": true,
 "gpsStatusEnabled": false,
 "heartbeatEnabled": true,
 "performanceMetricsEnabled": false,
 "runMode": "SCANNING",
 "initiatedTimestamp": "2023-10-19T13:07:17.757Z",
 "apiVersion": "1.0.0"
 }
}

    This message is the first initial message published once a successfuly connection is made. It provides basic information about the connected sensor and the messages that are current "subscribed to". This message is published once a minute and can be used as a heartbeat to ensure a client has a valid connection.

    New for API Version 2.5.0+

    Addition of the runMode attribute. See table below for valid runModes. The runMode is also published in TechniquePublication messages.

    runMode Description
    SCANNING Normal operations, SkyView is scanning for UAS
    TRANSMIT_LOCKOUT Scanning has been suspended due to transmitter being active (external ECM)
    VTX_PLAYBACK Scanning has been suspended, system has alocated radio resources to perform VTX video processing
    SPECTRUM_ANALYZER Scanning has been suspended, system has alocated radio resources to on-board Spectrum Analyzer

    Key API Changes for Version 2.5.8/2.6.8/3.0.8

    Addition of the blinkerBrightness attribute. Possible options are "HIGH, MED, LOW, OFF".
    Addition of the apiVersion attribut (potential future versioning of API).

    The TechniquePublication message provides detailed information regarding SkyView technique execution. The JSON content is made up of a message header and an enumeration of technique objects. A technique is generally a type of detector that is enabled and/or executing. These messages can be used to determine what detection techniques are currently enabled, if it is active (executing right now), and if a resulting detection is in progress. For SkyView-MPV2 Version 2.5.0, one or more techniques can be active at a given time. In addition, Version 2.5.0 publishes the TechniquePublication message once per second, even if there are no state changes to assist with more advanced UI technique status display requirements.

    Key API Changes for Version 2.5.0+

    • Addition of 3 new Detection Types (DigiXtend, Microhard, and HERO Loitering Munition). The example JSON has been updated to includes these new types.
    • Addition of the runMode attribute. See table below for valid runModes.

    Key API Changes for Version 2.5.3+

    • Addition of a new Detection Type (Orlan-10). The example JSON has been updated to includes these new types.

    Key API Changes for Version 2.5.6/2.6.3/3.0.X

    • Addition of 17 new Detection Types (DJI FPV, Feiyu Tech 605, Futaba FASST 2.4, Microhard UHF, Autel Nano/Micro, Freewave FGR3, Futaba FHSS 2.4, Herelink Video Transmitter, NTSC 2.4GHz Video, DJI Lightbridge GCS, Express LRS (R9M, Crossfire), Pixhawk (RFD, Holybro, 3DR), SIYI, DigiXbee, Spektrum).

    New for API Version 2.5.8/2.6.8/3.0.8

    • Renamed Autel Nano/Micro to Autel Skylink
    • Addition of 3 new Detection Types (FIMI, Graupner, Swellpro Splash).

    New for API Version 2.5.9/2.6.9/3.0.9

    • Addition of new Detection Types (REMOTEID_BLUETOOTH).
    • DJI_FPV and Feiyu Tech 605 techniques have been removed.
    • Pixhawk (RFD, Holybro, 3DR) and legacy Pixhawk have been combined into a single technique called Pixhawk

    New for API Version 2.5.14/2.6.14/3.0.14

    • DigiXtend and DigiXbee have been combined into a single technique called Digi.
    runMode Description
    SCANNING Normal operations, SkyView is scanning for UAS
    TRANSMIT_LOCKOUT Scanning has been suspended due to transmitter being active (external ECM)
    VTX_PLAYBACK Scanning has been suspended, system has alocated radio resources to perform VTX video processing
    SPECTRUM_ANALYZER Scanning has been suspended, system has alocated radio resources to on-board Spectrum Analyzer

    Key Elements

    Element Name Description
    techniqueLabel The user-friendly name of the technique
    techniquename The internal name of the technique (not intended for end users)
    isActive Boolean that indicates if the technqiue is executing now
    isDetected Boolean that indicates if the technqiue is currently detecting a UAS signature

    DetectionPublication

    DetectionPublication JSON Message: Non-Precision Detection Result

    
{
  "DetectionPublication": {
    "systemName": "skyview",
    "systemSerial": "SVMPV2-9000",
    "header": {
      "messageId": "5234c8a0-f264-43be-9e8f-b82b7ba44e00",
      "messageType": "DetectionPublication",
      "timestamp": "2021-10-05T17:13:56.969Z",
      "signature": null,
      "originator": "sv-controller"
    },
    "omniDetections": [
      {
        "detectionType": "FOXHIGH",
        "detectionLabel": "5.8GHz Video",
        "signalType": "UAS",
        "expired": false,
        "expirationSeconds": 40,
        "header": {
          "messageId": "d4080d4a-f582-422b-b910-6df8e0dcb960",
          "messageType": "sdrDetectionNotification",

          "signature": null,

        },

    The DetectionPublication message provides detailed information for active detection events produced by the SkyView system. The JSON content is made up of a message header and an array of detections based on detection type. Precision detections may contain additional information such as serial numbers and/or location/heading/attiude details.

    Key API Changes for Version 2.5.0

    • Some messages will include additional attributes (see example listsing). Of import, the centerFrequency and Carrier values may support advanced ECM techniques.

    Key API Changes for Version 2.5.6/2.6.3/3.0.X

    • Addition of new Detection Types as follows. The example JSON has been updated to includes these new types.
      • FEIYU_TECH_41AP
      • FREEWAVE_FGR3
      • NTSC_MID
      • EXPRESS_LRS
      • TARANIS_X8R
      • DIGI_XBEE
      • SPEKTRUM
      • FUTABA_FHSS
      • FUTABA_FASST
      • AUTEL_NANO_MICRO
      • HERELINK_HD_VTX
      • PIXHAWK_RFD3
      • LIGHTBRIDGE_HANDSET
      • SIYI_DK32
      • MICROHARD_NANO
      • MICROHARD_PICO
    • Changes in names for the following detection types
      • FOXHIGH is now NTSC_HIGH
      • FOXLOW is now NTSC_LOW
      • EVO is now AUTEL_EVO
      • DIGI is now DIGI_XTEND
      • SIK is now PIXHAWK
      • ST10 is now YUNEEC_TYPHOON
    • Detections are now grouped as "omniDetections" or "sectorDetections" so the same API can be used across both DIVR/DIVR MKII/DIV2 and MPV2/3. (note: on MPV2/3, sectorDetections will always be an empty array)
    • Removal of any discrete *demod* detection types. If a signal can provide precision details, they will be included with the base detection. Demodulation data has been seperated into the following interfaces (interface implementations are available in the table below):
      • Aircraft Location (aircraftLatitude, aircraftLongitude, aircraftAltitude)
      • Aircraft Heading (aircraftVelocityNorth, aircraftVelocityEast, aircraftVelocityUp)
      • Aircraft Attitude (aircraftPitch, aircraftRoll, aircraftYaw)
      • Pilot Location (pilotLatitude, pilotLongitude)
      • Home Location (pilotLatitude, pilotLongitude)
      • Target Location (targetLatitude, targetLongitude)

    Key Changes for API Version 2.5.8/2.6.8/3.0.8

    • Changed AUTEL_NANO_MICRO to AUTEL_SKYLINK
    • Addition of 3 new Detection Types (FIMI, GRAUPNER, SPLASH).

    Key Changes for API Version 2.5.9/2.6.9/3.0.9

    • Addition of new Detection Types (PAL_HIGH, PAL_MID, PAL_LOW, REMOTEID_BLUETOOTH).

    Key Changes for API Version 2.5.11/2.6.11/3.0.11

    • Removal of Detection Types (DJI_FPV, FRSKY_UHF, PIXHAWK_RFD3, FEIYU_TECH-41AP).
    • Addition of Detection Types (EXTENDED_EXPRESS_LRS, FISHERMAN, LANCET, NTSC_EXT, PAL_EXT, SUPERCAM).

    Key Changes for API Version 2.5.14/2.6.14/3.0.14

    • Many Detection Labels have been modified for clarity.
    • frequency field has been added to all SDR detections to indicate frequency range/band of detected signal

    Key Elements

    Element Name Description
    detectionType String representation of detection type (non user-friendly)
    detectionLabel String representation of user-friendly name of the signal that has been detected. This can be used for graphical displays or HMIs to communicate the active detection.
    detectionId String representation of unique detection ID. Each detection event is assigned a unique identifer by the system. This can be used by client logic for state management and observance of new detection events for a given type.
    createdTimeStamp DateTimeStamp created at the time the detection event object is created by the system. It can be used by the client to deterimne timing of detection events and aging functions

    GPSStatus

    Sample GPS Status publication from SkyView API:

    # GpsStatus notification is published when SkyView's internal GPS
    has received a revised position location.    

{
  "GpsStatus": {
    "systemName": "SVMPV3-9999",
    "systemSerial": "SVMPV3-9999",
    "header": {
      "messageId": "7a116deb-1e8f-4bef-bd23-e73f1939bdc3",
      "messageType": "gpsNotification",
      "timestamp": "2024-10-29T20:19:47.000Z",
      "signature": null,
      "originator": "passive_sdr"
    },
    "systemLatitude": "27.5384889",
    "systemLongitude": "-82.3943567",
    "systemAltitude": "13.552",
    "lastLocationUpdateTimestamp": "2024-10-29T20:19:47.000Z",
    "isFixedLocation": false,
    "systemHeading": "128.8051"
  }
}

    The GPSStatus message provides GPS status information generated by SkyView's internal GPS receiver. This information can be used by API consumers to perform sensot-to-target calculations or other sensor positional representations. NOTE: For many multi-sensor configurations (RADAR, CAMERA, and SkyView), a central GPS source is defined. In those configurations, SkyView's GPS Publications may be ignored.

    Key Changes for API Version 2.5.14/2.6.14/3.0.14

    • Addition systemHeading element (indicates heading in 0-259.999 degrees towards true north).

    Ground Tracks

    At this time, SkyView does not provide aggregated ground tracks for any aircraft. It is the responsibility of the API integrator to aggregate and sequence received detections for purposes of creating ground tracks. The information presented below summarizes the approach the SkyView Web UI takes to display this type of data.

    Within the SkyView Web UI, each received JSON detection is mapped into a new javascript detection object for purposes of displaying on the map and in various detection cards. Within the SkyView Web UI, detections contain the following fields relating to map markers and ground tracks:

    • flightpath[] - an array of lat/long points representing points on a polyline which are made up lat/long locations gleaned from previous detections.
    • markers - A collection lat/long of markers (Aircraft, Pilot, Home) indexed by a unique â€œserialâ€ for the current detection.

    When a JSON detection arrives, it is interrogated to determine if it contains positional data as follows:

    • Check to see if aircraftLatitude, aircraftLongitude values exist in the JSON and are non-zero values. Also check to see if abs(aircraftLongitude) <= 90. If all checks pass, it is assumed that this detection can be plotted on the map.
      • Create an â€œaircraftâ€ market element with the supplied lat/long
    • Similarly, check the incoming JSON for optional pilotLatitude/pilotLongitude as well as homeLatitude/Longitude and create associated â€œpilotâ€ and â€œhomeâ€ markers.

    Next the following logic is used to determine a unique identifier for the detection and store it in an internal â€œserialâ€ field.

    • If there is a JSON â€œserialâ€ value:
      • Assign the JSON â€œserialâ€ value to the internal object
      • If JSON contains detectionType starting with â€œLIGHTBRIDGEâ€ and there is a non-empty â€œtransmitterIdâ€, override the serial value with the â€œtransmitterIdâ€ field.
    • If there is no serial JSON value check for the following:
      • If JSON contains detectionType equals â€œWIFI_AEROSCOPEâ€ and there is a non-empty â€œidentifierâ€ property, assign this to the serial value
      • Else if the JSON contains property named â€œwifiClientIdâ€, use the wifiClientId as the serial
      • Else if the JSON contains property named â€œbaseStationIdâ€ and JSON detectionType equals â€œWIFI_REMOTE_IDâ€, use the baseStationId as serial.
      • Else if JSON contains detectionType starting with â€œLIGHTBRIDGEâ€ and there is a non-empty â€œtransmitterIdâ€, override the serial value with the â€œtransmitterIdâ€ field.
      • Else if the JSON contains detectionType equal â€œFSK_RMILECâ€ AND syncWord and transmitterId fields exist, use â€œsyncWordâ€ + â€œ-â€ + â€œtransmitterIdâ€ as the serial.

    SkyView Web UI contains a collection of â€œactiveâ€ detections. This array is used to track any detections that have been received within the last 60 seconds. An interval which runs every second scrubs the â€œactiveâ€ detects array searching for any expired detections (older than 60 seconds). If one is found, the detection is removed from the â€œactiveâ€ detects array.

    Once positional markers and unique identifying â€œserialâ€ data for an incoming detection have been determined, any â€œactiveâ€ detections already on the map are queried to see if there is a match. An â€œactiveâ€ detection is determined as a detect that has been received within the last 60 seconds.

    If there is a match finding a prior â€œactiveâ€ detection, data from the previous â€œactiveâ€ detect is copied into the newly created detection object.

    • All â€œflightPath[]â€ points are copied from the previous detect into the new detection object
    • The â€œaircraftLatitutdeâ€ and â€œaircraftLongitudeâ€ values of the previous detect are added at the tail of the â€œflightPath[]â€ array.

    Once the flightPath and markers have been created in the new detection object, all prior markers (Aircraft, Home, Pilot) and polyLines (ground track) are cleared from the map and the new points from the newly created detection object are painted on the map.

    Next, the newly created detection object is placed into the â€œactiveâ€ detects array (possibly replacing any prior detect with a matching â€œserialâ€ value.)
